## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=1)] Unexpected behaviour in cppref search

For some reason cppref search box is producing a browser search rather than the standard cpp type search. I am using Firefox, and there is no setting there to indicate this behaviour.
[BlueWhale](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:BlueWhale&action=edit&redlink=1) ([talk](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User_talk:BlueWhale&action=edit&redlink=1)) 05:04, 24 February 2021 (PST)

- Same here. Sends the search to Duck Duck Go for me which shows a bunch of unrelated content.

- Same. Search for "bitset" gives you results for drills and other tools, along with ads. pls rollback whatever messed up the search.


- And the worse is, we lost quick jump on search box typing. when I want to viewing the vector doc page, previously I just typing "vector" in search box and click the first suggestion, now I have to navigate to duckduckgo one more step.




## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=2)] Hiding previous versions of standard

Is it possible to hide everything unrelated to particular standard? It should be, because all the "before C++14, since C++14", "before C++17, since C++17" make pages hard to read. For example, look at [tuple constructor](cpp/utility/tuple/tuple.html). It would be nice to be able to hide everything unrelated to C++17 <or some other> standard. — Preceding unsigned comment added by [Hedede](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:Hedede&action=edit&redlink=1) ([talk](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User_talk:Hedede&action=edit&redlink=1) • [contribs](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Special:Contributions/Hedede)) 21:04, 12 December 2017 (PST)

- Yes, it is possible. You can go to
[Special:Preferences#mw-prefsection-gadgets](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Special:Preferences#mw-prefsection-gadgets)and enable the one labeled "<gadget-StandardRevisions>". That will give you a drop-down menu, and from that you can select your interested version. --[D41D8CD98F](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:D41D8CD98F&action=edit&redlink=1)([talk](User_talk%253AD41D8CD98F.html)) 00:58, 13 December 2017 (PST)

- That only works for logged-in users. I suspect most people visiting this wiki are not logged in, or even have an account. (There must be server stats for this but I don't know where they are.)
- It would be really useful to have that gadget visible to everyone. Is there a technical reason that prevents us from enabling a gadget for anonymous users? If not, is there non-technical reason we shouldn't do this?
[Guildd](User%253AGuildd.html)([talk](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User_talk:Guildd&action=edit&redlink=1)) 12:25, 19 January 2018 (PST)- The issue is that it isn't production quality. I recently spent a few hours testing it and
[made some notes](User%253AT._Canens/standard_revision_gadget_notes.html)on issues.[T. Canens](User%253AT._Canens.html)([talk](User_talk%253AT._Canens.html)) 13:15, 19 January 2018 (PST)- I wonder if we could put these issues to
[https://github.com/p12tic/cppreference-doc/issues](https://github.com/p12tic/cppreference-doc/issues)because it's so easy to lose them here. --[P12](User%253AP12.html)14:52, 7 June 2019 (PDT)

- I wonder if we could put these issues to

- The issue is that it isn't production quality. I recently spent a few hours testing it and


## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=3)] Usefulness of translated sites

Does anyone have strong feelings about the usefulness of the non-english subsites?

I've gotten a non-trivial amount of feedback from non-english speakers saying that the autotranslated content on those sites is at best useless (it's not very readable and quickly falls out of sync with the english-language content) and at worst disruptive (it can contaminate search results, making it harder for good results to bubble to the top).

People have been making changes to the non-english subsites, but at a very low rate compared to the english site. I don't like the idea of throwing out the translation work that people have done, but at some point the costs may outweigh the benefits.

Thoughts? --[Nate](User%253ANate.html) ([talk](User_talk%253ANate.html)) 10:05, 13 July 2016 (PDT)

- I only heard bad things about the non-English cppreference as well. --
[Cubbi](User%253ACubbi.html)([talk](User_talk%253ACubbi.html)) 11:33, 13 July 2016 (PDT)

- There has been significant amount of work in at least Russian and Chinese wikis and I think the content there is useful, especially given that we don't let search engines index autotranslated pages. The Chinese seems to be very active
[even now](http://zh.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Special:%E6%9C%80%E8%BF%91%E6%9B%B4%E6%94%B9&limit=500&days=90), although it's single person effort currently. Having said that the rest of the wikis are indeed not attracting interest and are unlikely to take off. I think we could export the content, backup it and shutdown the wikis. If someone thinks he wants to contribute significant amount of time, I could fire up a wiki with the archived content on a personal server on a personal domain for a month and during that time it would become clear if the contributor was serious or only talking. --[P12](User%253AP12.html)03:07, 1 February 2017 (PST)- Hmm, do we want to make a decision on this? Shut down everything but en (of course), zh, and ru? I have an
[AWB](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WP:AWB)bot set up to transform the piles of language links into {{[langlinks](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Template:langlinks)}}, but if we are doing this then that should probably wait.[T. Canens](User%253AT._Canens.html)([talk](User_talk%253AT._Canens.html)) 22:03, 3 July 2017 (PDT)- OTOH, if we convert to using the template, then we can globally suppress links to the removed languages in the template instead of cleaning up every page, and resurrecting a language - should we ever need to do that - can also be globally done in the template with a few edits. So maybe we should do the transformation anyways...
[T. Canens](User%253AT._Canens.html)([talk](User_talk%253AT._Canens.html)) 22:12, 3 July 2017 (PDT)

- OTOH, if we convert to using the template, then we can globally suppress links to the removed languages in the template instead of cleaning up every page, and resurrecting a language - should we ever need to do that - can also be globally done in the template with a few edits. So maybe we should do the transformation anyways...

- Hmm, do we want to make a decision on this? Shut down everything but en (of course), zh, and ru? I have an

A few years late to the party. I've been working to bring the Spanish version up to date, I have a few hours a week, but in case this discussion pops up again, don't shut the sites down. Eventually the idea is to promote es.cppreference.com in universities in Spain, Mexico. Latin America.
[ticotico](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:Ljestrada&action=edit&redlink=1) ([talk](User_talk%253ALjestrada.html)) 16:41, 19 March 2020 (PDT)

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=4)]

We've decided - I think - on merging {{[noexcept](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Template:noexcept)}} into the applicable function signatures, but there's no easy way to see which pages haven't been processed yet. What do people think of the following:

- Using
[Special:ReplaceText](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Special:ReplaceText), replace all current uses of {{[noexcept](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Template:noexcept)}} with a tracking template - say, {{[unreviewed noexcept](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Template:unreviewed_noexcept)}} - which looks just like {{[noexcept](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Template:noexcept)}} but has a hidden tracking category added to it. - We can then process the pages in the category and remove processed pages from the category, until it eventually becomes empty.

We could probably also do something similar with the <!--CWG 1234-->-style DR markers, most of which probably should go to {{[dr list item](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Template:dr_list_item)}}. [T. Canens](User%253AT._Canens.html) ([talk](User_talk%253AT._Canens.html)) 23:35, 30 March 2017 (PDT)

- I think some (many?) of the hidden DR comments are there to tell the future editors why the text differs from published pre-DR standard. Great idea for the noexcept migration though. --
[Cubbi](User%253ACubbi.html)([talk](User_talk%253ACubbi.html)) 06:28, 31 March 2017 (PDT)- I think it still makes sense to systematically review all the DR comments, though, to ensure that everything is in the DR list. We can still keep them after the review.
[T. Canens](User%253AT._Canens.html)([talk](User_talk%253AT._Canens.html)) 10:46, 31 March 2017 (PDT)- true. I started reviewing all DRs manually when DR list was invented (that's what
[User:Cubbi/Sandbox](User%253ACubbi/Sandbox.html)is about), but it fell to the bottom of priority list. --[Cubbi](User%253ACubbi.html)([talk](User_talk%253ACubbi.html)) 10:56, 31 March 2017 (PDT)

- true. I started reviewing all DRs manually when DR list was invented (that's what
- Also, do we want to keep the "Exceptions" section afterwards for simple cases (where we don't have anything to add beyond some combination of (none) and just {{
[noexcept](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Template:noexcept)}})? I'm not sure I see much point in keeping them.[T. Canens](User%253AT._Canens.html)([talk](User_talk%253AT._Canens.html)) 10:55, 31 March 2017 (PDT)

- I think it still makes sense to systematically review all the DR comments, though, to ensure that everything is in the DR list. We can still keep them after the review.

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=5)] Exact match in search results

When searching, if there is only one hit the site automatically redirects to that page. ([http://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?search=distance](../mwiki/index.php@search=distance.html))

When there are multiple results including an exact match, it does not automatically forward, although the exact match is listed on top. ([http://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?search=std%3A%3Alist](../mwiki/index.php@search=std%253A%253Alist.html))

This is particularly annoying since quite a lot of searches have two results, one in std and one in std::pmr for example (try searching for vector).

Would there be an easy way to (locally/using an extra GET argument?) change this behaviour, so that it always opens the first page on exact matches?

Also, I'm often too lazy to type the std:: part, but when searching 'set' for example, I usually just want the std::set.

[Ragnar](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:Ragnar&action=edit&redlink=1) ([talk](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User_talk:Ragnar&action=edit&redlink=1)) 04:25, 2 May 2017 (PDT)
Ragnar

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=12)] P0777R1/decay/remove_cvref

P0777R1's changes from [std::decay](cpp/types/decay.html) to std:remove_cvref are behavioral no-ops, even though they might increase compiler throughput. I think revboxing the changes gives them more prominence than they deserve. Possible options I can think of:

- Keep the revboxen as is, even though they don't alter the behavior in any way.
- Drop them and use
`remove_cvref`

throughout even for pre-C++20 features. - Drop them and keep using
`decay`

for pre-C++20 features (keep`remove_cvref`

for new features in C++20 and later). - Drop them and use remove_cv_t<remove_reference_t<...>> for pre-C++20 features

Thoughts? [T. Canens](User%253AT._Canens.html) ([talk](User_talk%253AT._Canens.html)) 15:40, 19 December 2017 (PST)

- New revisions of standards are made in order to be used by programmers. For me, I try to keep using the latest. For examples, differing standard is not a big problem (at least, not
*so*convincing to me). A resolution that meets most of demands is to show expressions in different standards, for example: use**remove_cvref**in all examples (including pre-C++20 ones) and comment something like "Pre-C++20 can use**decay(...)**(or so) instead" so most of the users can find their interesting stuff. --[LittleFlower](User%253ALittleFlower.html)([talk](User_talk%253ALittleFlower.html)) 18:35, 23 December 2017 (PST)

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=16)] another minor search bug

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=18)] Adding StandardRevisions and `cppreference.com` link to vector skin

I've enabled the `Vector` skin to make the list of languages available in the left bar, because I'm from Spain and sometimes I accidentally enter to the Spanish autotranslated version of the site, usually from google searchs. So it's comfortable to me to just click to the English version to get out of there.

The problem is, each time I search for something and move to any other part of the site besides main page, I have to go back to the manual page manually. However, the built-in styles have a the very useful `cppreference.com` link to come back to main page, that is missing in vector.

Also, I've enabled the StandardRevisions gadget and it only works for the built-in styles as well. Is it possible to add support for going back to the main page and the StandardRevisions gadget to the vector style? [Peregringlk](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:Peregringlk&action=edit&redlink=1) ([talk](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User_talk:Peregringlk&action=edit&redlink=1)) 02:36, 13 September 2019 (PDT)

- It looks like support for the StandardRevisions switcher has been enabled for Vector, so that's handled. 👍

- To provide a link back to the main page, the simplest solution would seem to be editing
[MediaWiki:sidebar](MediaWiki%253ASidebar.html)to include** mainpage|mainpage-description

at the top of the first list section. That's normally part of the default sidebar, but was removed for some reason. Since the sidebar is only shown in Vector, which doesn't show the "cppreference.com" link at the top of the page, restoring it should be unproblematic I would think?

- (The messages
[Mediawiki:mainpage](MediaWiki%253AMainpage.html)and[Mediawiki:mainpage-description](MediaWiki%253AMainpage-description.html), which are currently undefined and therefore defaulting to "Main Page" and "Main page", respectively) can also be set to customize the link. Setting[Mediawiki:mainpage-description](MediaWiki%253AMainpage-description.html)to "cppreference.com" would cause the sidebar link to match the top-of-page link on the custom skin(s). It is possible to localize system messages, for example the default/current[Mediawiki:mainpage-description/es](MediaWiki%253AMainpage-description/es.html)for the Spanish site is "Página principal". Though if it's going to be set to "cppreference.com" that probably doesn't even need localization.)

- Another alternative (or, really, an additional possibility independent of the first suggestion) would be to create a logo image for the site, which could be shown at the top of the sidebar. Currently the logo (which links back to the main page) is present in the Vector rendering, but it's being suppressed in the site CSS because the logo image is still set to the
[eyeball-searingly hideous default placeholder](../mwiki/skins/common/images/wiki.png). --[FeRDNYC](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:FeRDNYC&action=edit&redlink=1)([talk](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User_talk:FeRDNYC&action=edit&redlink=1)) 08:13, 28 October 2021 (PDT)

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=21)] Proposal for Dark-Mode Theme

Recently StackOverflow launched a Dark Theme(beta) that has been very well received and well implemented. They are currently taking making final tweaks to any of the pages that still have contrast issues, etc.. However, the dark-mode on SO has been brilliant. Eye-strain is greatly reduce which is one of the main benefits. Would Cppreference consider a similar addition of a dark-mode that would provide a choice between light and dark mode that the user could choose through their settings? [Drankinatty](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:Drankinatty&action=edit&redlink=1) ([talk](User_talk%253ADrankinatty.html)) 02:36, 4 April 2020 (PDT)

- Until then, I highly recommend the
[Deluminate](https://chrome.google.com/webstore/detail/deluminate/iebboopaeangfpceklajfohhbpkkfiaa)extension, it works great with cppreference, as well as Stack Exchange and more-or-less every other website I browse. Whilst we're at it, I propose adding a widescreen variant too, which I'm currently doing with Stylus with the CSS:`#content, #cpp-head-first, #cpp-head-second, #footer, .mw-geshi, .de1 { width: auto !important; }`

--[Ybab321](User%253AYbab321.html)([talk](User_talk%253AYbab321.html)) 07:56, 4 April 2020 (PDT)- I recently looked for acceptable extensions for Firefox. All required excess privileges. Some, like "DarkView" requeted the ability to clear browsing history and delete cookies -- not what you would expect in a dark reader. Seems implementing a dark-mode by cppreference.com for the mediawiki interface would be the safest option -- even if it takes more time to implement. Four years on, this is still a needed addition. The StackOverflow dark-mode model is a good model to look at for implementation, colors, etc..
[Drankinatty](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:Drankinatty&action=edit&redlink=1)([talk](User_talk%253ADrankinatty.html)) 21:04, 23 August 2024 (PDT)

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=22)] Where are level 2 headings?

Pages on this site tend to not have level 2 headings even when there are level 3 headings in them. (Examples: [cpp/preprocessor](cpp/preprocessor.html), [cpp/types](cpp/utility/rtti.html), [cpp/string/basic_string](cpp/string/basic_string.html), [cpp/thread/mutex/mutex](cpp/thread/mutex/mutex.html), [c/preprocessor](c/preprocessor.html), [c/string/byte](c/string/byte.html).) (Sometimes even level 3 is skipped.) Why is that? It kinda bothers me and, I suppose, is not perfect from the point of view of accessibility ([a relevant article](https://habr.com/ru/company/mailru/blog/532268/) (in Russian)) and understanding of content by web-crawlers. (My guess is that H2 elements are by default styled to be quite big and have a bottom border which would look ugly on pages with a lot of short top-level sections. But surely this can be fixed by using a custom style sheet.) — [Radix](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:Radix&action=edit&redlink=1) ([talk](User_talk%253ARadix.html)) 02:12, 12 April 2020 (PDT)

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=27)] Linking to WG21 and C++ draft

I think it might be useful to add links to WG21 papers that proposed a specific topic.

Maybe a link to the C++ draft could also be helpful?

What do you think?

If you agree, what format would you use?


Example std::string::starts_with

WG21 paper: [https://wg21.link/P0457R2](https://wg21.link/P0457R2)

C++ draft: [http://eel.is/c++draft/string.starts.with](http://eel.is/c++draft/string.starts.with)

Defect report: [https://cplusplus.github.io/LWG/issue3040](https://cplusplus.github.io/LWG/issue3040)


The papers can (sometimes) be found on the language version page or the compiler support page.

[https://en.cppreference.com/w/cpp/20](cpp/20.html)

[https://en.cppreference.com/w/cpp/compiler_support](cpp/compiler_support.html)

But adding it to the specific topic page makes it easier to trace the history of the topic.


Links to defect reports are already available for some topics.

E.g. [https://en.cppreference.com/w/cpp/string/basic_string/find](cpp/string/basic_string/find.html)


[WimLeflere](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:WimLeflere&action=edit&redlink=1) ([talk](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User_talk:WimLeflere&action=edit&redlink=1)) 12:15, 16 June 2020 (PDT)

- not sure detailed record-keeping of WG21's activities is well aligned with the core goal of being a resource to programmers: note how those defect reports are there when they are behavior-changing, as in, the programmer may encounter old behavior. Likewise, compiler_support is about what a programmer may or may not use given their toolset.
- One thing I could see as useful is being able to go from the page about a specific language/library feature to its compiler support status/evolution. but how could that be maintained? compiler_support works as it's a single page many people (including people working on the compilers) visit and care about. --
[Cubbi](User%253ACubbi.html)([talk](User_talk%253ACubbi.html)) 13:41, 16 June 2020 (PDT)

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=29)] constexpr specified revboxes

I think it's getting increasingly important to address the revboxing of C++20 function declarations that are only different by having `constexpr`

specified. I dislike how [string ctor](cpp/string/basic_string/basic_string.html) is presented, I like how [tuple ctor](cpp/utility/tuple/tuple.html) is presented, and I propose we switch to the latter as a convention. Anyone care to weigh in on this? --[Ybab321](User%253AYbab321.html) ([talk](User_talk%253AYbab321.html)) 10:40, 9 August 2020 (PDT)

- one functional difference is that if you use the language version pulldown, string ctor looks a whole lot neater compared to the tuple ctor. Someone has to make the gadget respect (constexpr since c++20) --
[Cubbi](User%253ACubbi.html)([talk](User_talk%253ACubbi.html)) 12:20, 9 August 2020 (PDT)


So here's what I think is the current and desirable presentation:

**Current:**

| (1) | ||
basic_string(); explicit basic_string( const Allocator& alloc ); |
(until C++17) | |
| basic_string() noexcept(noexcept( Allocator() )) : basic_string( Allocator() ) {} |
(since C++17) (until C++20) |
|
| constexpr basic_string() noexcept(noexcept( Allocator() )) : basic_string( Allocator() ) {} |
(since C++20) | |

**Desirable:**

Default (Diff) view:

| (1) | ||
| basic_string(); explicit basic_string( const Allocator& alloc ); |
(until C++17) | |
| constexpr basic_string() noexcept(noexcept( Allocator() )) : basic_string( Allocator() ) {} |
(since C++17) (constexpr since c++20) |
|

<gadget-StandardRevisions> in C++98/03 - C++14:

| (1) | ||
| basic_string(); explicit basic_string( const Allocator& alloc ); |
||

<gadget-StandardRevisions> in C++17:

| (1) | ||
| basic_string() noexcept(noexcept( Allocator() )) : basic_string( Allocator() ) {} |
||

<gadget-StandardRevisions> in C++20:

| (1) | ||
| constexpr basic_string() noexcept(noexcept( Allocator() )) : basic_string( Allocator() ) {} |
||

I think the desirable presentation can be achieved by:

1. add .t-dcl-constexpr-before { display: none } to [MediaWiki:common.css](MediaWiki%253ACommon.css.html)

2. change [MediaWiki:Gadget-standard_revisions.js](MediaWiki%253AGadget-standard_revisions.js.html) as indicated in the following patch (These are the minimum changes that "work". I made no attempt to make the additions follow the organization of the original code.):

| patch |
|---|
--- old +++ new @@ -1575,10 +1575,14 @@ StandardRevisionPlugin.prototype.prepare = function() { if (this.is_prepared) { return; } + this.constexpr_before = $('.t-dcl-constexpr-before'); + + this.constexpr_before.removeClass('t-dcl-constexpr-before'); + // initialize scopes this.root_scope = Scope.create_root($('#mw-content-text').first()); this.child_scopes = []; var self = this; @@ -1600,10 +1604,12 @@ self.prepare_all_li(scope, num_map); } }); + this.constexpr_before.addClass('t-dcl-constexpr-before'); + this.is_prepared = true; }; /** Utility function. Takes an jQuery object containing an array of elements that may or may not contain revision marker. @@ -1749,12 +1755,17 @@ be visible and reveals those that no longer need to be hidden (if any). */ StandardRevisionPlugin.prototype.on_selection_change = function() { this.prepare(); var rev = parseInt(this.select.val()); + this.tracker.to_rev(rev); + if (this.curr_rev !== Rev.DIFF && rev === Rev.DIFF) { + this.constexpr_before.css('display', 'none'); + } + // special treatment for rev boxes if (this.curr_rev === Rev.DIFF && rev !== Rev.DIFF) { this.for_all_scopes(function() { this.rev_tables.each(function() { $(this).addClass('stdrev-rev-hide'); |

3. update all pages to use the new t-dcl-constexpr-before class.

(After the first two steps, you can visit [playground](playground.html) to see the new presentation.)

--[D41D8CD98F](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:D41D8CD98F&action=edit&redlink=1) ([talk](User_talk%253AD41D8CD98F.html)) 07:01, 5 June 2021 (PDT)

- I really want to see this integrated, I'm happy to start editing the pages to use the new class if we can get this CSS+script merged --
[Ybab321](User%253AYbab321.html)([talk](User_talk%253AYbab321.html)) 05:21, 12 June 2021 (PDT) - Bump <_<; --
[Ybab321](User%253AYbab321.html)([talk](User_talk%253AYbab321.html)) 03:23, 8 July 2021 (PDT)

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=30)] BaseCharacteristic vs *base characteristic*

I'm seeing two different uses of this term. - It was originally spelled "BaseCharacteristic" in the standard before it was editorially changed to "base characteristic", so we ended up with a mix. I'll do a global search/replace.

- Hi, Javier.

- The
[std::format](cpp/utility/format/format.html)family is not implemented yet by**gcc/clang**(not sure about**cl**). To run the examples locally one can use the original[fmt](https://fmt.dev/latest/index.html)library, or better, use[gotbolt online compiler](https://godbolt.org)choosing the**fmt**library from the list of additional libraries and compile with flag`-std=c++20`

. - As to the cppreference's Online compilers, the following local discussion can shed the light on:
[online compiler](MediaWiki_talk%253AGadget-ColiruCompiler.html). Note, that the online-compilers are the same - the latest available on Coliru - gcc-v10.2 (and clang-5.0) now. Cubbi has fixed the version's title by changing the[script (gadget)](MediaWiki%253AGadget-coliru_compiler.js.html)for English version. The same could be done for other languages/sites. For instance, on Spanish es.cppreference.com[this file](https://es.cppreference.com/w/MediaWiki:Gadget-coliru_compiler.js)may be updated (s/"9.2"/"10.2", or just plain copy from English version would be enough, but admin rights are necessary).


A Bonus: cppreference online compier version checker

The complaints against the change will be wildly underrepresented, users will just find another reference site that has a cogent interface. Any "sample" that relies on casual site users going to the additional effort to create an account just to provide feedback is statistically invalid.

*far*from the only problem with the old search. Several of them are[discussed here](Cppreference_talk%253AFAQ.html#Search_on_site). Including...- Search was limited to a fixed number of matches (I think 20?) when there were often far more. Without a way to sort, if your desired match would be somewhere off the end of the list it was simply inaccessible.
- It was impossible, with the old search, to match any articles with titles that contain characters reserved in HTML / HTTP queries, such as an
`operator<<`

of some class, e.g..`basic_string::operator<<,>>()`

(DuckDuckGo does...*better*, with that. It looks like it ignores the <<, and just matches "operator" — but you can at least see the matches beyond the first page, unlike with the old search. Given the number of matches for "operator" on the site, the one you want is very likely to**not**be right up front.)

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=37)] Recent Changes Partially Obscure SearchBox with [View|Edit|History|Actions]

Sometime in the past week or two, changes made to this site cause the searchbox to be partially obscured by the [View|Edit|History|Actions] tabs. The searchbox size is now about twice the size it was. This is using Firefox 78.7esr. The only times I've seen this before had to do with Gtk+2 to 3 changes, but I don't see how that applies to a website. I have captured an image of what I see. It is posted at [https://paste.opensuse.org/51101549](https://paste.opensuse.org/51101549) (link good for 30 days)
[Drankinatty](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:Drankinatty&action=edit&redlink=1) ([talk](User_talk%253ADrankinatty.html)) 14:37, 24 February 2021 (PST)

- It looks like the issue is the
`box-sizing: border-box`

styling being applied to various page structural elements. The stanza in question looks like this, in the output CSS (when unminified):

div#cpp-head-first,div#cpp-head-second,div#content,div#footer { margin: 0 auto; position: relative; width: 780px; -moz-box-sizing: border-box; box-sizing: border-box }

- I just can't figure out where that's
*coming from*! It's not in[MediaWiki:Common.css](MediaWiki%253ACommon.css.html), and if there's a stylesheet file for the Cppreference2 skin I can't find it. But, disable that`box-sizing: border-box`

rule and everything fits correctly again. -
[Here's a userstyle](https://userstyles.org/styles/199156/cppreference-fix-page-header-element-overlapping)I just published to userstyles.org, which can be installed to fix the layout issue. --[FeRDNYC](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:FeRDNYC&action=edit&redlink=1)([talk](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User_talk:FeRDNYC&action=edit&redlink=1)) 04:14, 10 March 2021 (PST) - Setting "border:inherit" to the search text input and buttons make them fit within the design. No clue why the border is set to 10px, it must be for the rest of the wiki design. --
[70.54.171.187](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Special:Contributions/70.54.171.187)10:17, 10 March 2021 (PST)- @IP User: Technically that's true, but mostly because
`border: inherit`

resets the border width of those elements to 0. At that point the`box-sizing: border-box`

has no effect, because borderless elements are the same size no matter how you measure. Therefore, agreed — that change does also serve as a workaround for the problem. - Better, though (IMHO) to remove the ill-advised box-sizing rule, which makes everything fit the layout as-is. That way there's no need to sacrifice the current
`2px`

(not 10) borders on the search elements. --[FeRDNYC](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:FeRDNYC&action=edit&redlink=1)([talk](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User_talk:FeRDNYC&action=edit&redlink=1)) 16:14, 10 March 2021 (PST)

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=46)] Install MediaWiki Extension:TemplateSandbox?

The MediaWiki standard [Extension:TemplateSandbox](https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/Extension:TemplateSandbox) is handy not so much for the *sandbox* ability itself, but for a related feature it brings with it: The ability to preview the results of a template edit *in situ* on any page requested, prior to saving the edit and making it live.

The extension adds a field to the editor view (when editing in a namespace configured in `$wgTemplateSandboxEditNamespaces`

), offering to "Preview page with this template". There you can type any page title (presumably one which transcludes the template being edited), and it'll present a rendered view of the page as if your changes had been made live, but **without** them actually being made live yet.

Especially on sites where templates are heavily-used, deeply nested, intricately designed, or sparsely documented — and cppreference hits the quadfecta(?) by meeting **all four** of those criteria — it beats the more traditional "Edit, Save, Panic, Adjust, Save, Revert" loop that even experienced template coders often find themselves falling into, when attempting to make changes to live templates. As such, it also helps less-experienced editors make changes more confidently, and lowers the barrier to entry for new contributors to get involved in maintaining the site's frontend infrastructure.

Any possibility this highly-useful extension could find its was into the local MediaWiki install? Thx! -- [FeRDNYC](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:FeRDNYC&action=edit&redlink=1) ([talk](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User_talk:FeRDNYC&action=edit&redlink=1)) 21:02, 28 October 2021 (PDT)

- This seems like a reasonable request, but it looks like TemplateSandbox requires MW 1.33+ -- once we find time to upgrade the system, I think we can install that template. --
[Nate](User%253ANate.html)([talk](User_talk%253ANate.html)) 06:28, 29 October 2021 (PDT)

- @Nate: The current version
[actually requires 1.35+](https://gerrit.wikimedia.org/r/plugins/gitiles/mediawiki/extensions/TemplateSandbox/+/3f2ae2d9006a538935e942c122cdbd71d0934713), the Extension page is out of date. ## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=48)]

The descriptions of singleton object are treated differently.

type and its singleton object described in the same page:

-
[cpp/utility/in_place](cpp/utility/in_place.html)(the page is named after one of their singleton objects) -
[cpp/memory/new/destroying_delete_t](cpp/memory/new/destroying_delete_t.html)(the page is named after its class)

type and its singleton object described in separate pages:

-
[cpp/utility/piecewise_construct_t](cpp/utility/piecewise_construct_t.html)and[cpp/utility/piecewise_construct](cpp/utility/piecewise_construct.html) -
[cpp/memory/allocator_arg_t](cpp/memory/allocator_arg_t.html)and[cpp/memory/allocator_arg](cpp/memory/allocator_arg.html) -
[cpp/memory/new/nothrow_t](cpp/memory/new/nothrow_t.html)and[cpp/memory/new/nothrow](cpp/memory/new/nothrow.html)

For example, in page [cpp/memory/new](cpp/memory/new.html), nothrow_t and nothrow are classified as a class and an object, however, destroying_delete_t and destroying_delete share the same page, as well as the same link, classified as a class.


Similar situations also occurred in function and its corresponding constants/helper classes, but with even worse cases, such as:

- function and its corresponding constants/helper classes described in the same page or separate pages
- a group of functions with similar goals or a common goal described in the same page or separate pages
- functions (of few relation) described alone, with their corresponding constants collected together in a general summary page

Not to mention their links in summary pages and code blocks. It is tough to conclude due to its complexity so we'd better reach a consensus before further modifications.
[Yaossg](User%253AYaossg.html) ([talk](User_talk%253AYaossg.html)) 01:56, 18 April 2022 (PDT)

- I think a justifiable direction would be to merge
[cpp/memory/new/nothrow_t](cpp/memory/new/nothrow_t.html)into[cpp/memory/new/nothrow](cpp/memory/new/nothrow.html): from programmer's point of view,`nothrow`

is what they see and write in C++ code, and`nothrow_t`

is perhaps useful to understand an error message or when exploring a standard library headers. Similar to how[std::to_chars_result](cpp/utility/to_chars.html)has little use outside the context of[cpp/utility/to_chars](cpp/utility/to_chars.html). --[Cubbi](User%253ACubbi.html)([talk](User_talk%253ACubbi.html)) 05:52, 18 April 2022 (PDT)

-
[cpp/utility/in_place](cpp/utility/in_place.html)remain unchanged -
[cpp/memory/new/destroying_delete_t](cpp/memory/new/destroying_delete_t.html)be renamed to[cpp/memory/new/destroying_delete](cpp/memory/new/destroying_delete_t.html) -
[cpp/utility/piecewise_construct_t](cpp/utility/piecewise_construct_t.html)be merged into[cpp/utility/piecewise_construct](cpp/utility/piecewise_construct.html) -
[cpp/memory/allocator_arg_t](cpp/memory/allocator_arg_t.html)be merged into[cpp/memory/allocator_arg](cpp/memory/allocator_arg.html) -
[cpp/memory/new/nothrow_t](cpp/memory/new/nothrow_t.html)be merged into[cpp/memory/new/nothrow](cpp/memory/new/nothrow.html) - Helpers and similar functions maintain the status quo, for further discussion.

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=53)] C++ SSE and SSE2 compiler settings, and their Floating Point effects.

I have been running C++ floating point tests using the Twilight Dragon Media C++ compiler for 64 bit Windows 10.

C++ starts by using IEEE 754 equation for floats and doubles, decimal and hexadecimal values, floating point arithmetic, if I have things right. See this at:

I have learned that when you compile in

A)
**float a = 0.1F;**

what you get is stored is

**0.100000001490116119384765625**

whereas when you compile in

B)
**double b = 0.1D;**

what you get stored is

**0.1000000000000000055511151231257827021181583404541015625**

Most of your floating point operators are these: +, -, *, /, %, ++n, --n, n++, n--, +=, -=, *=, /=, %=

Is there a GNU C++ switch that will turn off all of these floating point overflow and underflow values, both for assignment of the floating point data and arithmetic operator calculation for separate floating point data, too? How can this be acheived without adjusting the floating point source code at all?

- The OP posted it on SO
[as a question](https://stackoverflow.com/questions/72432681), instead of looking at existing answers, and self-deleted since then to[re-ask](https://stackoverflow.com/questions/72445688), but one of the helful comments on the original question was a link to[https://randomascii.wordpress.com/2012/03/21/intermediate-floating-point-precision/](https://randomascii.wordpress.com/2012/03/21/intermediate-floating-point-precision/)- worth a read --[Cubbi](User%253ACubbi.html)([talk](User_talk%253ACubbi.html)) 12:39, 31 May 2022 (PDT)

- The OP posted it on SO

#include <string>

code "<string>" will become a link to [cpp/header/string](cpp/header/string.html)

[example](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Template:example)}}, {{[source](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Template:source)}} etc), there is another list:[MediaWiki:Geshi-keyword-list-cpp](MediaWiki%253AGeshi-keyword-list-cpp.html).

- for links in pages with tags like {{
- I'm planning to participate in collecting most of new C++17/20/23 identifiers, when most of C++23 pages will be written (or earlier), and settling them in these two lists (as I once did before).

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=55)] Mistakes in set

Just found that [cpp/container/set](cpp/container/set.html) has the following mistakes:

- It mentions
`key_type`

, while[the standard says](https://eel.is/c++draft/container.requirements#container.node.overview-4)"using key_type = see below; // not present for set containers" - It specifies "iterator - Constant LegacyBidirectionalIterator to value_type" and "const_iterator - LegacyBidirectionalIterator to const value_type" while
[the standard says](https://eel.is/c++draft/container.requirements#associative.reqmts.general-6)"both iterator and const_iterator are constant iterators" so the description should be identical between iterator and const_iterator (the latter is the accurate one)

I write here because I'm not totally sure how to fix the relevant templates and anyway wanted this to be reviewed in case I misread it

[Yehezkelshb](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:Yehezkelshb&action=edit&redlink=1) ([talk](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User_talk:Yehezkelshb&action=edit&redlink=1)) 12:10, 8 December 2022 (PST)

- The standard citation you linked in your first point is regarding
, which correctly specifies "map containers only" for`node_handle``key_type`

. I agree with your second point, and on that note, though the standard says`set`

's`iterator`

and`const_iterator`

are both "constant iterators" (which means they don't model[LegacyOutputIterator](cpp/named_req/OutputIterator.html)), but I would prefer if we wrote "iterator to`const value_type`

", I don't*think*that's inaccurate. --[Ybab321](User%253AYbab321.html)([talk](User_talk%253AYbab321.html)) 15:11, 8 December 2022 (PST)

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=58)] Proposal: add [User:D41D8CD98F/append-support-info.js](User%253AD41D8CD98F/append-support-info.js.html) for all users

[User:D41D8CD98F/append-support-info.js](User%253AD41D8CD98F/append-support-info.js.html) is a script written by me. This script adds a section to the bottom of a page, which shows implementation support information relevant to this page.

Sample screenshots:

-
[cpp/language/delete](cpp/language/delete.html):[https://i.imgur.com/UdMLuUg.png](https://i.imgur.com/UdMLuUg.png) -
[cpp/language/data_members](cpp/language/data_members.html):[https://i.imgur.com/m1pjJWG.png](https://i.imgur.com/m1pjJWG.png) -
[cpp/coroutine/generator/~generator](cpp/coroutine/generator/~generator.html):[https://i.imgur.com/DknpcRD.png](https://i.imgur.com/DknpcRD.png) -
[cpp/numeric/special_functions/ellint_3](cpp/numeric/special_functions/ellint_3.html):[https://i.imgur.com/33q4Guh.png](https://i.imgur.com/33q4Guh.png)

I believe that this script is useful for all readers, and thus should be enabled for everyone. AFAIK the simplest way to achieve this is adding importScript('User:D41D8CD98F/append-support-info.js') to [MediaWiki:common.js](MediaWiki%253ACommon.js.html).

ping [User:Cubbi](User%253ACubbi.html), [User:Nate](User%253ANate.html), [User:P12](User%253AP12.html), [User:T. Canens](User%253AT._Canens.html)

--[D41D8CD98F](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:D41D8CD98F&action=edit&redlink=1) ([talk](User_talk%253AD41D8CD98F.html)) 23:00, 10 April 2023 (PDT)

- I was just thinking that we should have a table like this another day. But I'm a bit worried about this implementation - it would generate API queries on every page.
- Also, when I tried this on
[std::string_view](cpp/string/basic_string_view.html), it also had rows for`optional`

and`any`

. How does it decide which rows to pick?[T. Canens](User%253AT._Canens.html)([talk](User_talk%253AT._Canens.html)) 17:38, 13 April 2023 (PDT)- I noticed that API queries are cached for a month (due to the
`cache-control: max-age=2592000`

HTTP header), so I decided to make use of this, instead of making another layer of cache. - The script considers a row
*relevant*if- It links to the current page, or to a parent of the current page.
- It links to a header, and the current page is defined in that header (as indicated by the use of
[Template:dcl header](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Template:dcl_header)). - The current page contains a table of feature-test macros. In this case, the script looks up in
[cpp/feature test](cpp/experimental/feature_test.html)to find out which papers are relevant, and picks every row in[cpp/compiler support](cpp/compiler_support.html)that links to one of these papers.

- In the case of
`string_view`

, the script finds`__cpp_lib_string_view`

, determines that P0220R1 is relevant, and shows every row that links to P0220R1. --[D41D8CD98F](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:D41D8CD98F&action=edit&redlink=1)([talk](User_talk%253AD41D8CD98F.html)) 22:48, 13 April 2023 (PDT)

- I noticed that API queries are cached for a month (due to the

- I've managed to add such a feature using {{excerpt}}‐like inclusion. See:
-
[Template:compiler_support](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Template:compiler_support)edits: 182018, 182020, 182022

-
- I've {{excerpt}}ed "Contracts" support to
[Template:cpp/compiler_support/26/contracts](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Template:cpp/compiler_support/26/contracts)and included it in both[Template:cpp/compiler_support/26](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Template:cpp/compiler_support/26)and the following pages:-
[cpp/language/contracts](cpp/language/contracts.html#Support_status)v: 182019 -
[cpp/language/contract_assert](cpp/language/contract_assert.html#Support_status)v: 182023 -
[cpp/keyword/contract_assert](cpp/keyword/contract_assert.html#Support_status)v: 182024 -
[cpp/identifier with special meaning/pre](cpp/identifier_with_special_meaning/pre.html#Support_status)v: 182025 -
[cpp/identifier with special meaning/post](cpp/identifier_with_special_meaning/post.html#Support_status)v: 182026

-
- This solution does not require scripts, does not make excessive amount of API calls, and should not cause cache issues. Yet, it will require to manually adding "Support status" sections, and splits
[Template:cpp/compiler support/26](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Template:cpp/compiler_support/26)into multiple excerpts. The "compiler support" subtemplates can be proxied. Feel free to bikeshed, follow, or undo. I believe this solution should be close to or optimal.[Benio](User%253ABenio.html)([talk](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User_talk:Benio&action=edit&redlink=1)) 20:13, 18 March 2025 (PDT)- It's not like anyone is making excessive amount of API calls.
- As to splitting
[Template:cpp/compiler support/26](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Template:cpp/compiler_support/26)into multiple excerpts, I'm concerned that it will make it more challenging for inexperienced editors to update the support status (they need to go through another page, and it's not very discoverable), and also more challenging for people to monitor the support status (previously they only need to add[Template:cpp/compiler support/26](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Template:cpp/compiler_support/26)to the[watchlist](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Special:Watchlist), but now they need to find and watch every excerpt). --[D41D8CD98F](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:D41D8CD98F&action=edit&redlink=1)([talk](User_talk%253AD41D8CD98F.html)) 23:29, 18 March 2025 (PDT)


- @ Benio.
- Splitting into multiple excerpts is sub-optimal, as it also places a burden on maintainers to invent a new name for each "excerpt" and update such templates when another compiler adds support for a corresponding C++ feature.
- Our wiki system will become overwhelmed with such “excerpts”, one per each Compiler Support Table (CST) row, which will put an even higher load on the system than the
*automatic*`D41D8CD98F`

's JavaScript solution. - The “excerpt”, as it's implemented now, duplicates some information already available on documentation page: revision, feature description, and (FTM)* block - that's not ideal. :-)

- If not via an
*automatic*script, the "support status" could be implemented using a single (per table) combined script that contains all entries/rows and several MediaWiki switches accepting a few arguments. -
Another question: do the documentation pages truly require “support status” tables? It is debatable. The existing small FTM tables already link to the CSTs under the "Value" column. A potential improvement would be to add links to CSTs for those features that do not have FTMs. This could be implemented as a small box with a link and explanatory text, similar to this one: [

[CST](cpp/compiler_support/26.html#cpp_contracts_202502L)], with optional CSS styling. -
If "Support status" sections are deemed desirable, they should be distinct from the CST row. There is no point to show compilers that do not support a given feature. Only those compilers that at least partially support a feature should be displayed on the documentation page.

--[Space Mission](User%253ASpace_Mission.html)([talk](User_talk%253ASpace_Mission.html)) 06:03, 19 March 2025 (PDT)

- @ Benio.

- "If not via an automatic script, the "support status" could be implemented using a single (per table) combined script that contains all entries/rows and several MediaWiki switches accepting a few arguments."



- I believe it's less efficient due to recache trigger upon CS update, yet indeed more user friendly to update CS table itself. I do agree this could be a good compromise. The question that remains: Do we want a global Support status? I'll refrain from making such a decision.

- The situation with autolinks inside code blocks is now much better. The next step is to expand {{
[lc](https://en.cppreference.com/w/Template:lc)}} GeSHi[database](MediaWiki%253AAutolinker-definition-cpp.html)for auto-linking within non-code parts of pages. --[Space Mission](User%253ASpace_Mission.html)([talk](User_talk%253ASpace_Mission.html)) 17:43, 11 October 2023 (PDT)

- The situation with autolinks inside code blocks is now much better. The next step is to expand {{

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=62)] Zapping `[[`[nodiscard](cpp/language/attributes/nodiscard.html)]]

from declarations?

[nodiscard](cpp/language/attributes/nodiscard.html)]]

I don't see why we need to have those annotations that have no normative effect. Implementations are free to warn, or not warn, whether or not the attribute is present. So they just make the declarations noisier and add to cognitive overhead if we have a standard diff where the only difference is the annotation (which it is in a lot of places). [T. Canens](User%253AT._Canens.html) ([talk](User_talk%253AT._Canens.html)) 16:23, 22 February 2024 (PST)

- If
[P2422](https://wg21.link/P2422)and[P3122](https://wg21.link/P3122)are voted into the standard as DR, then we can strike out all of them. --[Xmcgcg](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:Xmcgcg&action=edit&redlink=1)([talk](User_talk%253AXmcgcg.html)) 18:06, 22 February 2024 (PST)

- Those papers are not particularly relevant. Even if the standard added nodiscard to every function declaration where MSVC has it, my opinion would not change. The attribute doesn't have any normative effect, and it's just noise from a documentation perspective. There are tons of incorrect ways to call a function, and discarding the result is almost always among the more benign of them - the behavior is still well-defined, after all. There's no reason to call out this particular form of mistake in the declaration - C++ declarations are hard enough to read already.
[T. Canens](User%253AT._Canens.html)([talk](User_talk%253AT._Canens.html)) 17:08, 24 February 2024 (PST)

- Those papers are not particularly relevant. Even if the standard added nodiscard to every function declaration where MSVC has it, my opinion would not change. The attribute doesn't have any normative effect, and it's just noise from a documentation perspective. There are tons of incorrect ways to call a function, and discarding the result is almost always among the more benign of them - the behavior is still well-defined, after all. There's no reason to call out this particular form of mistake in the declaration - C++ declarations are hard enough to read already.

- I agree with the direction. In fact, we can stop adding new [[nodiscard]] from now on. The worst case I am worrying about is that someone starts removing the existing [[nodiscard]]s but stops somewhere in the middle. For example, the constexpr additions are now presented in two ways: separate revisions and (constexpr since C++XX) marks, and I have no clue whether the progress has ever been tracked.



## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=63)] inconsistency in formatting exposition-only names in decl and other source code

New names are introduced in recent standards and some of them are exposition-only which are not part of the interface to the user. However, there is inconsistency in their formatting across pages, particularly in the decl part, which doesn't align well:

| class /* exposition-name */; |
(1) | (exposition only*) |
| class /* __exposition_name */; |
(2) | (exposition only*) |
| class exposition-name; |
(3) | (exposition only*) |
| class __exposition_name; |
(4) | (exposition only*) |

Is there a way to resolve this problem in unifying its format of naming or declaring exposition-only items? It would be nice if there is a template in wrapping such names inside dcl template to italicize it just like how

is automatically italicized on *boolean-testable*[cpp/concepts/predicate](cpp/concepts/predicate.html).

[Cooky](User%253ACooky.html) ([talk](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User_talk:Cooky&action=edit&redlink=1)) 19:42, 12 April 2024 (PDT)

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=64)] The (still uncreated) Contract Support page name has a typo: "cotract" instead of "contract"

The page points to cpp/cotract.

[ticotico](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:Ljestrada&action=edit&redlink=1) ([talk](User_talk%253ALjestrada.html)) 09:16, 22 February 2025 (PST)

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Talk:Main_Page&action=edit§ion=65)] Request to remove the extra line break in the protected Template:Title on the Chinese site.

[zh:Template:title](http://zh.cppreference.com/w/Template:title) was vandalized in June 2024, then locked after restoration, but the restored version introduced an unexpected line break (compare with [en:Template:title](http://en.cppreference.com/w/Template:title)), causing spacing issues in titles. Example: [zh:Cppreference:FAQ](http://zh.cppreference.com/w/Cppreference:FAQ). --[YexuanXiao](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User:YexuanXiao&action=edit&redlink=1) ([talk](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=User_talk:YexuanXiao&action=edit&redlink=1)) 09:00, 19 March 2025 (PDT)

## Source: https://cppreference.com/w/cpp/11.html

# C++11

[cpp](../cpp.html)

**C++11** is the second major version of C++ and the most important update since C++98. A large number of changes were introduced to both standardize existing practices and improve the abstractions available to the C++ programmers.

Before it was finally approved by ISO on 12 August 2011, the name 'C++0x' was used because it was expected to be published before 2010. It took 8 years between C++03 and C++11, so it has become the longest interval between versions so far. Since then, currently, C++ updates every 3 years regularly.

| This section is incomplete |

Following features were merged into C++11:

- From
[TR1](experimental.html): all of TR1 except[Special Functions](numeric/special_math.html). - From Boost:
[The thread library](atomic.html),,`exception_ptr`and`error_code`, iterator improvements (`error_condition`,`begin`,`end`,`next`)`prev` - From C: C-style Unicode conversion functions

## Contents |

## Source: https://cppreference.com/w/cpp/14.html

# C++14

From cppreference.com

<

[cpp](../cpp.html)C++14 is a minor version after the major version C++11, featuring mainly minor improvements and defect fixes. Its approval was announced on August 18, 2014. It was released on December 15, 2014.

Before its approval, C++1y is sometimes used to indicate its release in 2010s.

| This section is incomplete |

## Contents |

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=cpp/14&action=edit§ion=1)] New language features

-
[variable templates](language/variable_template.html) -
[generic lambdas](language/lambda.html) - lambda init-capture
- new/delete elision
-
[relaxed restrictions on constexpr functions](language/constexpr.html) -
[binary literals](language/integer_literal.html) -
[digit separators](language/integer_literal.html#Single_quote) -
[return type deduction for functions](language/function.html#Return_type_deduction_.28since_C.2B.2B14.29) -
[aggregate classes](language/aggregate_initialization.html)with default non-static member initializers.

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=cpp/14&action=edit§ion=2)] New library features

-
[std::make_unique](memory/unique_ptr/make_unique.html) -
[std::shared_timed_mutex](thread/shared_timed_mutex.html)and[std::shared_lock](thread/shared_lock.html) -
[std::integer_sequence](utility/integer_sequence.html) -
[std::exchange](utility/exchange.html) -
[std::quoted](io/manip/quoted.html) - and many small improvements to existing library facilities, such as
- two-range overloads for some algorithms
- type alias versions of type traits
- user-defined literals for
,`basic_string`and`duration``complex` - etc.

## Source: https://cppreference.com/w/cpp/17.html

# C++17

From cppreference.com

<

[cpp](../cpp.html)C++17 is a major version that follows the minor version C++14 and introduces new language and library features. The standard was published in December 2017.

The following features were merged into C++17:

- From the
[File System TS](experimental/fs.html): the[filesystem library](filesystem.html). - From the
[Library fundamentals v1 TS](experimental/memory.html): features, including[std::any](utility/any.html),[std::optional](utility/optional.html),[std::string_view](string/basic_string_view.html),[std::apply](utility/apply.html),[polymorphic allocators](memory.html#Allocators),[searchers](functional.html#Searchers). - From
[Library fundamentals v2 TS](experimental/lib_extensions_2.html):[std::void_t](types/void_t.html),[std::conjunction](types/conjunction.html),[std::disjunction](types/disjunction.html),[std::negation](types/negation.html),[std::not_fn](utility/functional/not_fn.html),[std::gcd](numeric/gcd.html),[std::lcm](numeric/lcm.html). - From
[Parallelism v1 TS](experimental/parallelism.html): features, including[execution policies](algorithm/execution_policy_tag_t.html),[std::reduce](algorithm/reduce.html),[std::inclusive_scan](algorithm/inclusive_scan.html),[std::exclusive_scan](algorithm/exclusive_scan.html), but removing`exception_list`

. - From
[Mathematical special functions IS](experimental/special_math.html):[mathematical special functions](numeric/special_math.html). - From C11:
[std::aligned_alloc](memory/c/aligned_alloc.html),[std::timespec_get](chrono/c/timespec_get.html).

| This section is incomplete |

##### [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Template:cpp/compiler_support/17&action=edit§ion=T-3)] Notes

- As of 2020-11-20, the latest release of Oracle Developer Studio
[is 12.6](https://www.oracle.com/application-development/technologies/developerstudio-component-matrix.html). Its[documentation](https://docs.oracle.com/cd/E77782_01/html/E77789/bkaje.html)does not mention C++17. - Cray compiler may have support for some features earlier than 11.0. That version is when it became a derivative of Clang, gaining all of the attendant language feature support of the base compiler. See
[Cray/HPE document S-2179](https://support.hpe.com/hpesc/public/docDisplay?docLocale=en_US&docId=a00123566en_us).

* - hover over a cell marked with the star * to see additional pop-up notes.

DR*nn* - the number *nn* after "DR" denotes target C++ revision the Defect Report is applied to, e.g., DR20 → C++20.

## Source: https://cppreference.com/w/cpp/20.html

# C++20

From cppreference.com

<

[cpp](../cpp.html)C++20 is a major version after C++17, featuring major features (concepts, modules, coroutines, and ranges) and other language and library features. The standard was published in December 2020.

`typename`

to disambiguate types in many contexts -
,`consteval``constinit` - Further relaxed constexpr
- Signed integers are 2's complement

# C++23

From cppreference.com

<

[cpp](../cpp.html)The current revision of the C++ standard.

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=cpp/23&action=edit§ion=1)] New language features

- New
[language feature testing macros](experimental/feature_test.html#Language_features) -
[Explicit object parameter](language/function.html#Explicit_object_parameter),[explicit object member functions](language/member_functions.html#Explicit_object_member_functions), a.k.a. "deducing this" ([P0847R7](https://wg21.link/P0847R7)) -
[Multidimensional subscript operator](language/operators.html#Array_subscript_operator)(e.g. v[1, 3, 7] = 42;) ([P2128R6](https://wg21.link/P2128R6)) - static operator[] (
[P2589R1](https://wg21.link/P2589R1)), static operator(), and static lambdas ([P1169R4](https://wg21.link/P1169R4)) - auto(x) and auto{x}:
[decay-copy](language/explicit_cast.html#Syntax)in the language ([P0849R8](https://wg21.link/P0849R8)) - Assumptions via new attribute
`[[`

([assume](language/attributes/assume.html)(*expression*)]][P1774R8](https://wg21.link/P1774R8)) - Attributes on
[lambda-expressions](language/lambda.html#Syntax)([P2173R1](https://wg21.link/P2173R1)) - Optional
[extended floating-point types](types/floating-point.html): std::float{16|32|64|128}_t, and[std::bfloat16_t](types/floating-point.html)([P1467R9](https://wg21.link/P1467R9)) - New preprocessor directives:
(`#elifdef`

,`#elifndef`

[P2334R1](https://wg21.link/P2334R1)), and(`#warning`[P2437R1](https://wg21.link/P2437R1)) -
[Literal suffix '](language/integer_literal.html#The_type_of_the_literal)for (signed)`Z`

'/'`z`

'[std::size_t](types/size_t.html)literals ([P0330R8](https://wg21.link/P0330R8)), e.g. auto ouz = 0uz; - White-spaces trimming before line splicing. (
[P2223R2](https://wg21.link/P2223R2)) - Simpler implicit move (
[P2266R3](https://wg21.link/P2266R3)) - Extending the lifetime of temporaries in range-based for loop initializer (
[P2718R0](https://wg21.link/P2718R0)) - CTAD from inherited constructors (
[P2582R1](https://wg21.link/P2582R1)) - Labels at the end of compound statements (
[P2324R2](https://wg21.link/P2324R2)), e.g.


- void f(int& x)

{

if (x)

goto END;

x = 42;

END:

}

- Alias declarations (using) in init-statements (
[P2360R0](https://wg21.link/P2360R0)), e.g.


- for (using T = int; T e : v)

/* ... */

- Make

more optional for lambda expressions (**()**[P1102R2](https://wg21.link/P1102R2)) - Narrowing contextual conversions to bool in static_assert and if constexpr (
[P1401R5](https://wg21.link/P1401R5)) - Make declaration order layout (of non-static class data members) mandated (
[P1847R4](https://wg21.link/P1847R4)) - Text encoding changes:
-
[Character sets and encodings](language/charset.html)([P2314R4](https://wg21.link/P2314R4)) - Consistent character literal encoding (
[P2316R2](https://wg21.link/P2316R2)) -
[Named universal character escapes](language/escape.html#Named_universal_character_escapes), e.g. "\N{CAT FACE}" for "🐱" ([P2071R2](https://wg21.link/P2071R2)) -
[Delimited escape sequences](language/escape.html), e.g. "\o{7777}", "\x{C0DE}", "\u{CAFE}" ([P2290R3](https://wg21.link/P2290R3)) -
[Support for UTF-8 as a portable source file encoding](language/translation_phases.html#Phase_1)([P2295R6](https://wg21.link/P2295R6))

-
-

##### [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=cpp/23&action=edit§ion=6)] General Utilities

-
[std::expected](utility/expected.html): a new vocabulary type to return a function's result () (`<expected>`[P0323R12](https://wg21.link/P0323R12),[P2549R1](https://wg21.link/P2549R1)) -
[std::move_only_function](utility/functional/move_only_function.html): a move-only callable wrapper ([P0288R9](https://wg21.link/P0288R9)) -

[std::byteswap](numeric/byteswap.html): reverses the bytes ([P1272R4](https://wg21.link/P1272R4)) -
[std::forward_like](utility/forward_like.html)([P2445R1](https://wg21.link/P2445R1)) -
[std::invoke_r](utility/functional/invoke.html): invokes a[Callable](named_req/Callable.html)object ([P2136R3](https://wg21.link/p2136r3)) -
[std::to_underlying](utility/to_underlying.html): a utility function to get the underlying value of enum ([P1682R3](https://wg21.link/P1682R3)) -
[std::unreachable](utility/unreachable.html): a function to mark unreachable code ([P0627R6](https://wg21.link/p0627r6)) - Monadic operations (
`transform`

,`or_else`

, and`and_then`

) for[std::optional](utility/optional.html)([P0798R8](https://wg21.link/P0798R8)) and[std::expected](utility/expected.html)([P2505R5](https://wg21.link/P2505R5)) -
[std::tuple](utility/tuple.html)is compatible with other tuple-like objects ([P2165R4](https://wg21.link/p2165r4)) - Adding default arguments for
[std::pair](utility/pair.html)'s forwarding constructor ([P2718R0](https://wg21.link/p2718r0)) -
[std::basic_common_reference](types/common_reference.html)specialization for[std::reference_wrapper](utility/functional/reference_wrapper.html)yielding reference types ([P2655R3](https://wg21.link/p2655r3))

- New range adaptors:
-

[P2164R9](https://wg21.link/p2164r9)) -

-
-

-
[ranges::starts_with](algorithm/ranges/starts_with.html)and[ranges::ends_with](algorithm/ranges/ends_with.html)([P1659R3](https://wg21.link/p1659r3)) -

[ranges::iota](algorithm/ranges/iota.html),[ranges::shift_left](algorithm/ranges/shift.html), and[ranges::shift_right](algorithm/ranges/shift.html): rangified versions of non-constrained algorithms ([P2440R1](https://wg21.link/p2440r1)) -
[ranges::fold_left](algorithm/ranges/fold_left.html)etc.:[range fold algorithms](algorithm/ranges.html#Constrained_fold_operations)([P2322R6](https://wg21.link/p2322r6))

-
- Rectifying constant iterators, sentinels, and ranges, that is,
[ranges::cbegin](ranges/cbegin.html)and other similar utilities returning constant iterators should be fully guaranteed even for shallow-const views (such as[std::span](container/span.html)) ([P2278R4](https://wg21.link/p2278r4)) - Making multi-param constructors of some views explicit (

-

[std::stack](container/stack.html)and[std::queue](container/queue.html)([P1425R4](https://wg21.link/p1425r4)) - Heterogeneous erasure overloads for associative containers (

## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=cpp/23&action=edit§ion=15)] Obsolete features

##### [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=cpp/23&action=edit§ion=16)] Removed features

- Garbage collection support and reachability-based leak detection. (
[P2186R2](https://wg21.link/P2186R2)) - Mixed wide string literals
[concatenation](language/string_literal.html#Concatenation)support, e.g., const auto* no = u"q" U"p" is ill-formed. ([P2201R1](https://wg21.link/P2201R1)) - Non-encodable wide character literals and multicharacter wide character literals, e.g. wchar_t x = 'db' is ill-formed. (
[P2362R3](https://wg21.link/P2362R3))

##### [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=cpp/23&action=edit§ion=17)] Deprecated features

##### [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=cpp/23&action=edit§ion=18)] Reverted deprecations

- The operator, (comma operator) in subscript expressions (but the semantics has been changed to support overloadable multidimensional subscript operator[]).
- Some C headers (the corresponding
`<*.h>`

headers for compatibility with C) ([P2340R1](https://wg21.link/P2340R1))

## Source: https://cppreference.com/w/cpp/compiler_support.html

# C++ compiler support

[cpp](../cpp.html)

| This page is maintained as best-effort and may lag behind most recent compiler releases. If you see something is out-of-date, please help us by updating it! |


The following tables present compiler support for new C++ features. These include accepted revisions to the standard, as well as various technical specifications:

## Contents |

#### [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=cpp/compiler_support&action=edit§ion=1)] Notes

* - hover over a cell marked with the star * to see additional pop-up notes.

DR*nn* - the number *nn* after "DR" denotes target C++ revision the Defect Report is applied to, e.g., DR20 → C++20.


## [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=cpp/compiler_support&action=edit§ion=2)] C++26 features

Note that this list may change, as the draft C++26/2c standard evolves.

# Compiler support for C++11

From cppreference.com

[cpp](../../cpp.html) |[compiler support](../compiler_support.html)* - hover over a cell marked with the star * to see additional pop-up notes.

DR*nn* - the number *nn* after "DR" denotes target C++ revision the Defect Report is applied to, e.g., DR20 → C++20.

##### [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=Template:cpp/compiler_support/17&action=edit§ion=T-3)] Notes

- As of 2020-11-20, the latest release of Oracle Developer Studio
[is 12.6](https://www.oracle.com/application-development/technologies/developerstudio-component-matrix.html). Its[documentation](https://docs.oracle.com/cd/E77782_01/html/E77789/bkaje.html)does not mention C++17. - Cray compiler may have support for some features earlier than 11.0. That version is when it became a derivative of Clang, gaining all of the attendant language feature support of the base compiler. See
[Cray/HPE document S-2179](https://support.hpe.com/hpesc/public/docDisplay?docLocale=en_US&docId=a00123566en_us).

## Source: https://cppreference.com/w/cpp/preprocessor.html

# Preprocessor

From cppreference.com

<

[cpp](../cpp.html)The preprocessor is executed at [translation phase 4](language/translation_phases.html#Phase_4), before the compilation. The result of preprocessing is a single file which is then passed to the actual compiler.

## Contents |

### [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=cpp/preprocessor&action=edit§ion=1)] Directives

The preprocessing directives control the behavior of the preprocessor. Each directive occupies one line and has the following format:

- the # character.
- a sequence of:

- a standard-defined directive name (listed
[below](preprocessor.html#Capabilities)) followed by the corresponding arguments, or - one or more
[preprocessing tokens](language/translation_phases.html#Phase_3)where the beginning token is not a standard-defined directive name, in this case the directive is conditionally-supported with implementation-defined semantics (e.g. a common non-standard extension is the directive #warning which emits a user-defined message during compilation)(until C++23), or - nothing, in this case the directive has no effect.

- a standard-defined directive name (listed

- a line break.

|
The |
(since C++20) |

Preprocessing directives must not come from macro expansion.

#define EMPTY EMPTY # include <file.h> // not a preprocessing directive

### [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=cpp/preprocessor&action=edit§ion=2)] Capabilities

The preprocessor has the source file translation capabilities:

-
compile parts of source file (controlled by directive #if, #ifdef, #ifndef, #else, #elif, #elifdef, #elifndef(since C++23), and #endif).[conditionally](preprocessor/conditional.html) -
text macros while possibly concatenating or quoting identifiers (controlled by directives #define and #undef, and operators # and ##).[replace](preprocessor/replace.html) -
other files (controlled by directive #include and checked with __has_include(since C++17)).[include](preprocessor/include.html) - cause an
or[error](preprocessor/warning.html)(since C++23) (controlled by directive #error or #warning respectively(since C++23)).[warning](preprocessor/warning.html)

The following aspects of the preprocessor can be controlled:

-
behavior (controlled by directive #pragma and operator _Pragma(since C++11)). In addition, some compilers support (to varying degrees) the operator __pragma as a[implementation-defined](preprocessor/impl.html)*non-standard*extension. -
available to the preprocessor (controlled by directive #line).[file name and line information](preprocessor/line.html)

### [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=cpp/preprocessor&action=edit§ion=3)] Defect reports

The following behavior-changing defect reports were applied retroactively to previously published C++ standards.

| DR | Applied to | Behavior as published | Correct behavior |
|---|---|---|---|
|

|
| |

## Source: https://cppreference.com/w/cpp/comments.html

# Comments

[cpp](../cpp.html)

Comments serve as a sort of in-code documentation. When inserted into a program, they are effectively ignored by the compiler; they are solely intended to be used as notes by the humans that read source code. Although specific documentation is not part of the C++ standard, several utilities exist that parse comments with different documentation formats.

## Contents |

### [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=cpp/comment&action=edit§ion=1)] Syntax

comment
|
(1) | ||||||||
comment
|
(2) | ||||||||

All comments are removed from the program at [translation phase 3](language/translation_phases.html#Phase_3) by replacing each comment with a single whitespace character.

### [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=cpp/comment&action=edit§ion=2)] C-style

C-style comments are usually used to comment large blocks of text, however, they can be used to comment single lines. To insert a C-style comment, simply surround text with

and **/***

; this will cause the contents of the comment to be ignored by the compiler. Although it is not part of the C++ standard, ***/**

and **/****

are often used to indicate documentation blocks; this is legal because the second asterisk is simply treated as part of the comment. C-style comments cannot be nested.
***/**

### [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=cpp/comment&action=edit§ion=3)] C++-style

C++-style comments are usually used to comment single lines, however, multiple C++-style comments can be placed together to form multi-line comments. C++-style comments tell the compiler to ignore all content between

and a new line.
**//**

### [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=cpp/comment&action=edit§ion=4)] Notes

Because comments [are removed](language/translation_phases.html#Phase_3) before the preprocessor stage, a macro cannot be used to form a comment and an unterminated C-style comment doesn't spill over from an #include'd file.

Besides commenting out, other mechanisms used for source code exclusion are

#if 0[std::cout]<< "this will not be executed or even compiled\n"; #endif

and

if (false) {[std::cout]<< "this will not be executed\n"; }

### [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=cpp/comment&action=edit§ion=5)] Example

#include <iostream> /* C-style comments can contain multiple lines */ /* or just one */ /************** * you can insert any *, but * you can't make comments nested */ // C++-style comments can comment one line // or, they can // be strung together int main() { // comments are removed before preprocessing, // so ABC is "1", not "1//2134", and "1 hello world" // will be printed #define ABC 1//2134[std::cout]<< ABC << " hello world\n"; // The below code won't be run // return 1; // The below code will be run return 0; }

Output:

1 hello world

## Source: https://cppreference.com/w/cpp/language/basics.html

# Basic concepts

This section provides definitions for the specific terminology and the concepts used when describing the C++ programming language.

A C++ program is a sequence of text files (typically header and source files) that contain [declarations](declarations.html). They undergo [translation](translation_phases.html) to become an executable program, which is executed when the C++ implementation calls its [main function](main_function.html).

Certain words in a C++ program have special meaning, and these are known as [keywords](../keywords.html). Others can be used as [identifiers](name.html). [Comments](../comments.html) are ignored during translation. C++ programs also contain [literals](expressions.html#Literals), the values of characters inside them are determined by [character sets and encodings](charset.html). Certain characters in the program have to be represented with [escape sequences](escape.html).

The *entities* of a C++ program are values, [objects](objects.html), [references](reference.html), [structured bindings](structured_binding.html)(since C++17), [result bindings](function.html#Postcondition_assertions)(since C++26), [functions](functions.html), [enumerators](enum.html), [types](type-id.html), class members, [templates](templates.html), [template specializations](template_specialization.html), [packs](parameter_pack.html)(since C++11), and [namespaces](namespace.html). Preprocessor [macros](../preprocessor/replace.html) are not C++ entities.

[Declarations](declarations.html) may introduce entities, associate them with [names](name.html) and define their properties. The declarations that define all properties required to use an entity are [definitions](definition.html). A program must contain only one definition of any non-inline function or variable that is [odr-used](definition.html#ODR-use).

Definitions of functions usually include sequences of [statements](statements.html), some of which include [expressions](expressions.html), which specify the computations to be performed by the program.

Names encountered in a program are associated with the declarations that introduced them using [name lookup](lookup.html). Each name is only valid within a part of the program called its [scope](scope.html). Some names have [linkage](storage_duration.html) which makes them refer to the same entities when they appear in different scopes or translation units.

Each object, reference, function, expression in C++ is associated with a [type](type-id.html), which may be [fundamental](types.html), compound, or [user-defined](classes.html), complete or [incomplete](incomplete_type.html), etc.

Declared objects and declared references that are not [non-static data members](data_members.html) are *variables *.

### [[edit](https://en.cppreference.com/mwiki/index.php?title=cpp/language/basic_concepts&action=edit§ion=1)] See also

|
|

# C++ keywords

[cpp](../cpp.html)

This is a list of reserved keywords in C++. Since they are used by the language, these keywords are not available for re-definition or overloading. As an exception, they are not considered reserved in [attributes](language/attributes.html) (excluding attribute argument lists).(since C++11)

- (1) — meaning changed or new meaning added in C++11.
- (2) — new meaning added in C++14.
- (3) — meaning changed or new meaning added in C++17.

- (5) — new meaning added in C++23.

[alternative way to represent standard tokens](language/operator_alternative.html). These keywords are also considered reserved in attributes (excluding attribute argument lists), but some implementations handle them the same as the others.(since C++11)
